I upgraded to a larger space when my monthly 5x5 price increased close to the 10x5 price; literally the next unit over.  However, after 6 months the fee increased an additional $50/month so I moved units to the 2nd floor for a lower price.  I've paid three admin fees total during each move due to the price bumps. It's difficult to reach the regional manager/director.

My grievances are:
1. there's only 1 day in the month in which a customer is able to move without being double charged, for two entire months (bad new policy for customers - absolutely no pro-rate)
2.  there's admin fees associated for changing units
3. every 6 months rent increases for customers
4. no access to moving carts after 6pm (threw out my back because of the additional lifting & carrying).

Best notes about this facility (random order):
1. Clean building
2. Climate controlled
3. Jasmaine< /text>

<name>Rebekah Brown<//name><date>1470781851204< /date><review>Clearing out of this place was a HUGE problem. Turns out there were break-ins, including my unit and the unit next to mine. Too bad I didn't find that out until right now because the way this business is run is shady and incompetent.

I came to my storage unit to pick up my bike. One front desk clerk told me that Public Storage had cut my lock because I was late on a payment. It seemed weird to me at the time, because when I had paid the month before, the woman on the phone told me that we weren't close to the timeframe of a lien. Anyway, the clerk told me that replacing the lock would be a $19 charge. Since it was cheaper for me to pro-rate my balance for the month and move out, I decided to do that. I was already pretty over this place at this point. I asked her if I needed to turn in my keys. She told me that I didn't need to, since the lock had been cut, and I could just throw them away. I paid my balance and came back two days later to move.

Well, it turns out that my lock hadn't been cut. Another lock had just been placed over it. Once they took the outer lock off, my original lock was underneath, except now I had no keys to open it. The clerk apologized and told me they'd cut my lock that night and I could come back the following day to clear out. She said she'd call me with a confirmation, which she never did.

I returned the next day anyway. My lock hadn't been cut. The clerk I'd spoken to the day before wasn't there, so a different person tried to reach the manager in charge of cutting the lock while I waited. After an hour, I gave up and asked if I could come back the next day. They assured me I could. They called me an hour later to tell me the lock had just been cut and I could return the next morning.

When I arrived, however, a third time, the lock still had not been cut. At this point, I was angry and my boyfriend was angry, because we'd been driving over an hour from where we live to come clear out of the unit. The clerk again called the manager to come cut the lock. Again, we waited. The manager arrived. My boyfriend, who was irate by this point, gets into screaming match with her.  She threatens to call the police and refuses to cut the lock, telling us to call a locksmith. I take him outside to calm down, and go back inside to offer a genuine apology to the manager and the clerk for the argument.

The manager agreed to cut my lock as long as my boyfriend wasn't present. We cut the lock, and I begin clearing out my unit. But...It looks funny. Things are thrown all over the place and all of the boxes have been opened. Stuff is definitely missing. At this point, I don't want to deal with another confrontation, and I'm really eager to get out of there. After I load everything into a cart, I notice that the fencing that normally covers the ceiling has been cut and bent back on the entire back side of the unit. Looks like a break in to me!

I go back downstairs and talk to yet another front desk clerk, explaining to him that it looks like my unit was broken into. He comes upstairs with me to verify and agrees. He explains that a month or so earlier, a man was caught breaking into the units on my floor. The unit next to mine had its front lock broken and he probably climbed over through the ceiling into mine. Insurance MIGHT cover my missing items, but also maybe not since THEY CANCELLED my insurance after my late payment (never mind the fact that when I paid the balance in full, they also charged extra for the late payment).

So, the clerk verifies my move-out (finally!), he gives me some insurance info for the break-in, and I go home. Pretty sucky situation. I already wish I'd never used Public Storage and am just so glad I never have to go back. Well, I get a phone call about an hour after I get home from the front desk. The clerk asks if I want him to close out my account. In order to do so, he says, I need to pay the balance on my unit. Ugh. I tell him that three different people have told me I don't owe any money for the days I waited. I have to drive again back for the receipt. THE WORST.<//review>< UserId.>

<Resp>None</Resp><user>105616935051199947863< /user>< text>
I ordered the shrimp PO boy, it came with coleslaw and Cajun fries, the fries were the best part. The sandwich had a total of 4 shrimp on it, just enough to call it a shrimp PO boy. the top layer of the sandwich was slathered in coleslaw which was heavy on dressing and light in cabbage, I had to take it off. Their menu is convoluted in its layout and just about nothing has a set price. Which is fine But what's the point of your menu if I have to check the giant blackboard anyways?
The fried pickles are amazing and netted them 1/2 another star, the atmosphere is pretty nice too. 1/2 star,  this rating is based on the po boy sandwich. If you can't deliver a good po boy, don't offer it.<//text>

<Resp>None</Resp><Text>This is the best WingStop I've ever been to. Note this is a little bit of a late review, by a couple months. Let me preface this by saying I'm from San Diego and we have several locations but they aren't in the best of areas and/or have staffing with the worst attitudes and terrible customer service skills.

With all that said, this location had some friendly staff who were very accommodating from the moment that I arrived to the moment I left.

The food was fresh... Now I know in all locations the food is always "made fresh".. but for some reason the wings and tenders at this location were more satisfying. The chicken was juicier and the sauces didn't taste watered down. The buffalo tenders were super sauced up and the lemon pepper/ parmesan wings had that heavy rub action. In fact, it reminded me of our first Wing Stop when it originally opened in San Diego. Even the fries took me back to my original experience.

They even had their drink supply fully loaded which is hard to come by in San Diego. When I order a combo they don't have anything yo drink other than sparkling water.

Last but not least the prices at this location are a little bit lower than what I'm used to paying. Which was just a bonus.

All in all, I couldn't find anything wrong on my visit. Thank you!<//Text>< time>
